Runtime and Database Isolation\r\n\r\nDo not run mutating Player/Quartermaster E2E until database isolation is proven.\r\n\r\nRequired:\r\n\r\n1. create uniquely named database copy;\r\n2. use explicit absolute `DATABASE_URL`;\r\n3. record server PID and port;\r\n4. store isolation nonce in copied DB;\r\n5. query nonce through application;\r\n6. record canonical DB path/hash/size/modification time;\r\n7. run mutations only on the copy;\r\n8. verify canonical DB remains unchanged.\r\n\r\nAn alternate worktree or port is not database isolation.\r\n\r\nIf proof fails:\r\n\r\n* stop mutation tests;\r\n* classify as environment failure;\r\n* do not continue by assumption.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 48. Validation Commands\r\n\r\nUse verified repository commands only.\r\n\r\nAt minimum run appropriate focused and full versions of:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nnpm run format:check\r\nnpm run lint\r\nnpm run typecheck\r\nnpm test\r\nnpm run assets:validate\r\nnpm run test:e2e\r\nnpm run build\r\nnpm run validate\r\n```\r\n\r\nOnly one validation owner runs the integrated full gate.\r\n\r\nDo not run multiple production builds or full E2E suites concurrently.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 53. Phase 3 Acceptance Criteria\r\n\r\nUnfurl the Tale is complete only when every condition below is satisfied.\r\n\r\n## Persistent host\r\n\r\n* One persistent Player progression host exists outside conditional section content.\r\n* It remains mounted across all six sections.\r\n* It owns authoritative Player presentation.\r\n* It does not become a second business-state store.\r\n* It restores section and focus.\r\n\r\n## Chapter release\r\n\r\n* Visible from all six sections.\r\n* Does not force navigation.\r\n* Required targets are host-local and unique.\r\n* Replay survives refresh.\r\n* Replay causes zero mutation.\r\n* Full mode completes in under 10,000 ms.\r\n* Gentle and reduced preserve meaning.\r\n* Fallback is readable.\r\n* Acknowledgment follows valid receipt only.\r\n\r\n## Event coverage\r\n\r\n* All 17 progression events have explicit typed policies.\r\n* All 102 full-mode event/section cases pass.\r\n* Every event has a global presentation.\r\n* Relevant sections receive at most one local enhancement.\r\n* Off-section absence cannot make an event invisible.\r\n* Duplicate event IDs do not replay.\r\n\r\n## Journal\r\n\r\n* First opening, reentry, replay, skip, interruption, completed archive and fallback end at `JOURNAL_READY`.\r\n* PageFlip handoff is stable.\r\n* Hidden source content never satisfies a scene.\r\n* Page turns expose lifecycle labels.\r\n* Focus and page index remain correct.\r\n\r\n## Section choreography\r\n\r\n* Map events animate only changed marker/path.\r\n* Artifact events use explicit source/destination handles.\r\n* Quest events animate only the affected quest/objective.\r\n* Log events use Motion row wrappers and GSAP ink children.\r\n* Finale events animate only changed requirement/mechanism state.\r\n* Pause/resume/undo reconcile globally and safely.\r\n\r\n## Replay\r\n\r\n* Every replayable Phase 3 presentation passes the full replay protocol.\r\n* Replay works after refresh.\r\n* Replay works from any section.\r\n* Replay uses immutable safe payloads.\r\n* Replay creates no story mutation or additional viewed receipt.\r\n\r\n## Audio\r\n\r\n* Audio begins only at semantic labels after preflight.\r\n* Sound failure is non-blocking.\r\n* Sound is never the only signal.\r\n* Duplicate events do not duplicate cues.\r\n\r\n## Motion policy\r\n\r\n* Full, gentle, product reduced, browser reduced and combined reduced reach equivalent semantic states.\r\n* Mode changes do not accidentally replay scenes or one-shot Lottie.\r\n* Reduced mode remains readable and interactive.\r\n\r\n## Accessibility\r\n\r\n* Keyboard access passes.\r\n* Focus restoration passes.\r\n* Live-region behavior passes.\r\n* No hidden PageFlip source is focusable.\r\n* No hover-only information exists.\r\n* Sound-independent meaning passes.\r\n\r\n## Lifecycle\r\n\r\n* Hosts, claims, runtimes, listeners and timers return to baseline.\r\n* No stale scene instance remains.\r\n* No leaked focus trap remains.\r\n* No detached-node writes occur.\r\n* Twenty-cycle stress tests pass.\r\n\r\n## Requirement completion\r\n\r\n* Every accepted Phase 3 MX requirement is implemented or has an explicit external blocker.\r\n* Every accepted Phase 3 OA requirement is implemented or has an explicit external blocker.\r\n* No architecture-only placeholder is falsely marked complete.\r\n* Zero accepted Phase 3 requirements remain unmapped.\r\n* Zero accepted Phase 3 requirements silently move to another phase.\r\n* All later-phase requirements remain preserved.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 54. Explicitly Out of Scope\r\n\r\nDo not broadly implement Phase 4 platform work during this phase:\r\n\r\n* modern sign-in polish;\r\n* Invitation Ceremony;\r\n* Player Library;\r\n* Captain Library;\r\n* New Voyage wizard;\r\n* waiting-room platform choreography unless required for Player journal handoff;\r\n* Studio animation;\r\n* shell-wide platform transitions.\r\n\r\nDo not broadly implement Phase 5 authored assets:\r\n\r\n* production Journal Clasp `.riv`;\r\n* production Voyage Compass `.riv`;\r\n* production Finale Mechanism `.riv`;\r\n* production Invitation Seal `.riv`;\r\n* final Lottie asset revisions;\r\n* final PageFlip runtime completion beyond required Phase 3 integration.\r\n\r\nDo not broadly implement Phase 6 final optimization and polish.\r\n\r\nDo not:\r\n\r\n* replace GSAP with Motion;\r\n* replace Motion with GSAP;\r\n* replace StPageFlip;\r\n* fake Rive with unlabeled CSS while claiming Rive completion;\r\n* expose private event content;\r\n* change story logic;\r\n* change authoritative progression semantics;\r\n* create a competing application;\r\n* start Phase 4 automatically.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 55. Repeated replay-button activation should be request-debounced, not confused with live-event deduplication.\n\nA failed mandatory automatic attempt remains explicitly retryable. Retry uses the stored immutable envelope through a controller method; it does not masquerade as a newly received event.\n\n## State machine\n\n```text\nqueued\n  → preparing\n  → presenting\n  → normalizing\n  → terminal\n\nterminal:\n  completed\n  presented-fallback\n  skipped-readable\n  duplicate\n  interrupted\n  failed-retryable\n  cancelled\n  revoked\n```\n\nController-wide modes should separately track `online`, `offline-paused`, `reconciling`, and `revoked`.\n\nEvery accepted request receives exactly one terminal progression receipt. The canonical Tall Tale invitation/playthrough runtime and the six-section cinematic `Campaign` runtime are separate event stacks with no adapter between them.\n\n## Current end-to-end flow\n\n### Legacy six-section Player experience\n\n1. Quartermaster selects one of the 17-producing actions in [Quartermaster.tsx](C:/Users/kkids/Documents/Codex_TreasureHunt/src/components/gm/Quartermaster.tsx:80).\n2. Confirmation starts a Captain-side animation whose `operation` POSTs `/api/gm/action`, not `/api/gm/commands`, in [Quartermaster.tsx](C:/Users/kkids/Documents/Codex_TreasureHunt/src/components/gm/Quartermaster.tsx:332).\n3. [action/route.ts](C:/Users/kkids/Documents/Codex_TreasureHunt/src/app/api/gm/action/route.ts:5) validates GM session, CSRF, and `gmActionSchema`, then calls `executeProgressionAction`.\n4. [progression.ts](C:/Users/kkids/Documents/Codex_TreasureHunt/src/server/progression.ts:93) transactionally:\n\n   - saves pre-action state for undo;\n   - mutates authoritative campaign/domain rows;\n   - increments `Campaign.currentSequence`;\n   - inserts `ProgressEvent`;\n   - inserts `CampaignSnapshot`;\n   - inserts `AdminAuditLog`.\n\n5. After commit, `toClientEvent` applies the per-event allowlist in [visibility.ts](C:/Users/kkids/Documents/Codex_TreasureHunt/src/domain/visibility.ts:11), then `publishCampaignEvent` emits through the process-local `EventEmitter` in [events.ts](C:/Users/kkids/Documents/Codex_TreasureHunt/src/lib/events.ts:9).\n6. [events/route.ts](C:/Users/kkids/Documents/Codex_TreasureHunt/src/app/api/player/[campaignSlug]/events/route.ts:8) authenticates `PlayerAccess`, replays persisted rows after a sequence, then subscribes to the in-process bus.\n7. [PlayerExperience.tsx](C:/Users/kkids/Documents/Codex_TreasureHunt/src/components/player/PlayerExperience.tsx:507) receives SSE, deduplicates with an in-memory set, serializes arrival through `eventChain`, and maps the 17 types to scenes through `sceneByEvent` at line 44.\n8. For `CHAPTER_RELEASED`, it reloads the persisted safe snapshot, waits for the presentation receipt, and POSTs `/viewed` only when the receipt permits acknowledgment.\n9. For the other 16 types, the director receipt is discarded: there is no persisted presentation acknowledgment, failure recovery, or replay history.\n\nTruth boundary: committed state/event/audit rows prove persistence. The Quartermaster toast and `delivery: \"PUBLISHED\"` do not prove that a Player received or presented an event.\n\n### Hardened command path, currently not used by the UI\n\n`/api/gm/commands` and `executeAdminCommand` add expected-sequence conflicts, idempotency, `CommandExecution`, correlation IDs, failed audit rows, and persisted results in [admin-command.ts](C:/Users/kkids/Documents/Codex_TreasureHunt/src/server/admin-command.ts:156). The E2E tests exercise this API directly in [command-center.spec.ts](C:/Users/kkids/Documents/Codex_TreasureHunt/tests/e2e/command-center.spec.ts:42).\n\nThe production Quartermaster buttons still use `/api/gm/action`, so they receive none of those protections. `commandCapability()` is defined but used only by its unit test; neither command route enforces it.\n\n## Event-family coverage\n\n| Phase 3 family | Current producer | Player scene | Persistence | Ack / replay |\n|---|---|---|---|---|\n| `CHAPTER_RELEASED` | `RELEASE_CHAPTER` | `chapter-release` | State + event + snapshot + audit | Persisted per campaign/device/event; latest release replay only |\n| `CHAPTER_SOLVED` | `MARK_SOLVED` | `mark-solved` | Yes | Receipt discarded; no replay |\n| Artifact award / silhouette / connection | `AWARD_ARTIFACT`, `REVEAL_ARTIFACT_SILHOUETTE`, `CONNECT_ARTIFACTS` | `artifact-award`, `artifact-connection` | Yes | No persisted presentation ack/replay |\n| Map location / route | `REVEAL_MAP`, `REVEAL_ROUTE` | `map-reveal`, `route-draw` | Yes | No persisted presentation ack/replay |\n| Quest discovery / update / completion | `DISCOVER_SIDE_QUEST`, `UPDATE_SIDE_QUEST`, `COMPLETE_SIDE_QUEST` | `quest-discovery`, `quest-complete` | Yes | No persisted presentation ack/replay |\n| Annotation / log entry | `ADD_JOURNAL_ANNOTATION`, `ADD_LOG_ENTRY` | `log-entry` | Yes | No persisted presentation ack/replay |\n| Finale tease / requirement | `TEASE_FINALE`, `UPDATE_FINALE_REQUIREMENT` | `finale-tease`, `finale-requirement` | Yes | No persisted presentation ack/replay |\n| Pause / resume / undo | `PAUSE`, `RESUME`, `UNDO_LAST` | `pause`, `resume`, `undo` | Yes | No persisted presentation ack/replay |\n\nThe mapping is visually exhaustive, but it is a `Partial<Record<ProgressEventType, ...>>`, not the Phase 3 exhaustive typed policy that must fail when a required event lacks a declaration.\n\n## Phase 3 section comparison\n\n### Section 22 — Quartermaster bridge\n\nSupported:\n\n- real server operation and pending UI;\n- transactional authoritative event creation;\n- Player-safe SSE;\n- Captain receives event ID and sequence;\n- process-local live publication plus database catch-up.\n\nMissing or unsafe:\n\n- visible UI does not perform command-specific `/preview` preflight;\n- visible UI has no expected sequence, idempotency key, target/reason, or correlation ID;\n- its `AdminAuditLog.correlationId` is normally null;\n- no capability enforcement;\n- only chapter release acknowledges after a Player receipt;\n- command and Player presentations cannot be correlated end-to-end;\n- Captain “Player synchronized” diagnostics are not presentation truth.\n\nThere is also a serious post-commit failure window: `executeProgressionAction` commits, publishes the Player event, and only then builds the response snapshot. If snapshot/response work fails, the Captain can receive an error while the Player has already received real success. The hardened path likewise marks `CommandExecution` only after the progression transaction/publication, so a crash or update failure can leave a committed Player event with a failed or permanently running Captain receipt.\n\n### Section 26 / 37 — Replay\n\nCurrent replay is limited to the latest `CHAPTER_RELEASED` through `PublicSnapshot.latestChapterReleasePresentation`. It correctly reconstructs safe content from authoritative state and does not reuse the raw narrative SSE payload.\n\nMissing:\n\n- Player-facing persisted history for the other replayable families;\n- replay after more than the latest chapter release;\n- immutable payload/version projection for every family;\n- source distinction in the transport (`live`, `reconnect`, `replay`);\n- the full 12-step protocol for each replayable scene;\n- persisted proof that replay generated no viewed receipt.\n\n### Section 30 — Offline and reconnect\n\nMissing:\n\n- unseen event calculation from persisted per-event presentation receipts;\n- readable multi-event reconciliation summary;\n- mandatory-event queue after reconnect;\n- explicit gap detection;\n- stale-event policy;\n- legacy Player access-revocation signal;\n- retry after a failed non-chapter presentation.\n\n`PlayerExperience` opens SSE with `after = snapshot.sequence`. Consequently, events already represented in the initial snapshot are treated as synchronized and never automatically presented, except for the special latest-chapter recovery.\n\n### Sections 38–39 — one-shot and interruption\n\nCurrent scopes are inconsistent:\n\n- `seenEvents` and automatic-attempt sets: component mount only;\n- journal introduction: browser tab/session storage per campaign;\n- chapter ceremony: campaign + local device + event ID;\n- ordinary viewed content: `PlayerAccess` + content type/key;\n- canonical journal `lastEventSequence`: profile preferences or local storage.\n\nA non-chapter event is inserted into `seenEvents` before presentation. If presentation fails, the duplicate is suppressed for the rest of that mount. There is no duplicate receipt, retry state, or persisted failure receipt.\n\nOnly chapter presentation failures are surfaced. Other interruption outcomes are swallowed after the director returns.\n\n## Missing request/receipt envelope fields\n\n`ClientProgressEvent` currently contains only:\n\n```text\nid, type, sequence, payload, releaseAt\n```\n\nThe bridge still needs a typed request/envelope carrying or resolving:\n\n- `source: live | reconnect | replay`;\n- correlation/command execution ID;\n- event payload/schema version;\n- actor/source identity class;\n- `reversesEventId` and supersession identity;\n- priority, mandatory status, replay policy, and one-shot scope;\n- return section/current section;\n- requested motion policy;\n- authoritative snapshot/state version;\n- presentation attempt/scene instance linkage.\n\n`PresentationReceipt` has scene instance, host, outcome, labels, target report, acknowledgment eligibility, and cleanup, but lacks event sequence/correlation and is only held in memory. Presentation telemetry is also an in-memory capped diagnostic recorder, not a durable Player receipt.\n\n`STATE_REVERTED` is especially under-specified: persistence knows `reversesEventId`, but Player serialization exposes only `reversedType`, so it cannot render the required exact previous/current identities.\n\n## Transport and race risks\n\n- Both SSE routes query missed rows and only then subscribe to the in-process bus. An event committed/published in that interval is missed until a later reconnect.\n- Live fan-out is process-local; another application instance will not receive the event.\n- `eventChain` preserves arrival order, not authoritative sequence order; there is no buffer for gaps/out-of-order arrival.\n- Duplicate IDs are silently dropped rather than producing the required duplicate receipt.\n- `latestSequence` advances on receipt before successful presentation.\n- Presence posts `acknowledgedSequence: snapshot.sequence` in [PlayerExperience.tsx](C:/Users/kkids/Documents/Codex_TreasureHunt/src/components/player/PlayerExperience.tsx:536). GM status therefore can report zero lag even when a scene failed or was never attempted.\n- `/viewed` accepts event presentation acknowledgments only for `CHAPTER_RELEASED` in [viewed/route.ts](C:/Users/kkids/Documents/Codex_TreasureHunt/src/app/api/player/[campaignSlug]/viewed/route.ts:19).\n- Legacy SSE validates access only when the stream opens and has no terminal revocation mechanism.\n\n## Canonical Tall Tale platform split\n\nThe canonical invitation/runtime stack uses:\n\n```text\nInvitation\n-> PlayerProfile\n-> PlaythroughMembership\n-> TaleSession\n-> TaleSessionEvent\n-> /api/play/sessions/[sessionId]/events\n-> TallTaleJournalSession\n```\n\nThis stack has hashed invitation credentials, player identity, membership checks, and identity revocation polling. It is not connected to `Campaign`, `ProgressEvent`, `PlayerAccess`, or `PlayerExperience`.\n\nIts persisted `TaleSessionEvent` envelope is richer—published version, block, source, idempotency key, sequence, and optional correlation—but the Player SSE strips it to ID/type/sequence/time. The Player state API exposes only the latest 40 events and removes correlation/version/idempotency details.\n\nAdditional confirmed gaps:\n\n- `captainSessionAction` can persist several events in one transaction but emits only the returned event.\n- `TallTaleJournalSession` initializes `processedSequence` to the current snapshot sequence and persists `lastEventSequence` without a cinematic receipt.\n- concurrent catch-up loads can collapse several events into one latest pending notice;\n- canonical event vocabulary (`blockEntered`, `artifactGranted`, `sessionPaused`, etc.) has no declared projection to the Phase 3 17-event policy;\n- no per-event viewed/presentation receipt or cinematic replay model exists.\n\nPhase 3 therefore needs an explicit architecture decision: either adapt authoritative `TaleSessionEvent` into the 17 presentation families and mount the six-section host in the canonical Player runtime, or formally retain the legacy campaign stack and document why it remains authoritative. Silently implementing only the legacy bridge would leave real invitation-based Players outside Phase 3.\n\n## Focused test recommendations\n\n1. receipt, not transport/state cursor | Only valid live/reconnect terminal outcome writes once | Chapter release only |\n\n## Critical confirmed gaps and races\n\n1. Both SSE routes perform `findMany()` before registering `eventBus.on()`. An event emitted in that gap is lost until a later reconnect.\n\n2. `PlayerExperience` marks an event seen and advances `latestSequence` before presentation completes. A failed non-chapter event is therefore consumed across refresh without retry.\n\n3. Arrival order, not authoritative sequence, controls `eventChain`. Live SSE happens to send backlog ascending, but the client does not protect against out-of-order live delivery.\n\n4. `playEvent()` unconditionally aborts `presentationRun.current`. A user-started replay can abort an authoritative live scene, violating live-over-replay priority.\n\n5. The Director’s numeric priority can cancel an active lower-priority scene but cannot reorder its existing FIFO tail. A newly arrived critical scene can still sit behind previously queued medium work.\n\n6. Duplicate IDs are discarded before Director playback. No duplicate receipt or integrity-collision evidence is produced. Same ID with different type, sequence, or payload is not distinguished from a benign redelivery.\n\n7. Only chapter release consumes `decideChapterPresentation()` and persists `ViewedCeremony`. Other production scene contracts declare Player acknowledgment ownership, but no durable acknowledgment follows.\n\n8. `PlayerPresence.acknowledgedSequence` is populated from `snapshot.sequence`, not presentation receipts. GM diagnostics can report “synchronized” while a mandatory ceremony failed or remains unacknowledged.\n\n9. Current replay is not the immutable event payload required by Phase 3. `projectChapterReleaseReplay()` preserves event identity/title but composes narrative/objective/riddle from current readable chapter state.\n\n10. Replay history is limited to the latest chapter release. There is no all-event replay surface or replay after later releases.\n\n11. `TallTaleJournalSession.load(event)` changes an event sequence to `max(event.sequence, currentSequence)` while retaining its old event type. A quick pause/resume can announce “paused” at the resume sequence and then discard the actual resume event as stale.\n\n12. `pendingEvent` is a single slot. Concurrent `load()` calls can overwrite missed events rather than queue them.\n\n13. Tall Tale initialization sets `processedSequence` directly to current session sequence and persists it. Previously unseen events are consumed without a reconciliation summary or mandatory-scene queue.\n\n14. Journal reading state is stored inside the whole `PlayerProfile.preferences` JSON document. Concurrent tabs can read the same old value and overwrite each other; a page-only write can regress persisted `lastEventSequence`.\n\n15. Tall Tale pause/resume changes status before idempotency is checked in `appendEvent()`. Reusing an old pause key after a later resume can change status back to paused without creating a corresponding new event.\n\n16. Legacy undo exposes only `reversedType` to Players. It lacks exact affected identities and before/current values. The original event is not visibly superseded, so repeated undo selection can target stale history.\n\n17. Tall Tale SSE revocation closes the source, but the offline polling effect immediately continues `load()` every five seconds and the Retry button remains active.\n\n18. Legacy campaign SSE validates access only when opening. It has no periodic revocation check and can continue streaming after access removal.\n\n19. Revocation does not clear replay payloads, state, DOM, audio, local persistence, or queued work.\n\n20. Session-authorized media responses use `Cache-Control: public, max-age=31536000, immutable`. Private/revealed assets can survive revocation in browser or shared caches.\n\n21. Both event serializers expose event type, ID, sequence, and timing for event classes outside the Phase 3 Player allowlist. Tall Tale state also returns all recent event types/source types with sanitized payloads. Operational/private metadata remains inferable.\n\n## Recommended authority split\n\nPhase 3 should keep four truths separate:\n\n1. Business truth: one canonical progression aggregate and durable ordered event log.\n2. Player-safe immutable event truth: a versioned replay envelope created transactionally with the authoritative event.\n3. Presentation truth: one terminal controller receipt per accepted attempt.\n4. Acknowledgment truth: an idempotent server record keyed by Player/membership, event ID, and policy version.\n\nClient state should separately track:\n\n- last transport-received sequence;\n- last state-reconciled sequence;\n- pending/active/terminal presentation records;\n- last persisted presentation acknowledgment.\n\nNeither snapshot sequence nor reading position may masquerade as presentation acknowledgment.\n\nFor reconnect, retrieve an authorization-consistent snapshot, Player-safe events through its sequence, and acknowledgment statuses. Merge by ID, detect identity collisions, sort by sequence, show a bounded summary, then queue mandatory events. The SSE server must either register/buffer before reading backlog or perform a second catch-up read after listener registration.\n\nFor revocation:\n\n- abort Director/controller work;\n- clear the queue and retry timers;\n- stop audio and ambient work;\n- discard replay/state payloads and private DOM;\n- clear approved local/session caches;\n- render a terminal state;\n- make session/invitation media `private, no-store`;\n- never treat revocation as ordinary reconnecting.\n\n## One-shot scope recommendation\n\nThis remains a product-policy decision but should be explicit:\n\n- First journal introduction: currently conflicts—legacy is once per browser tab/campaign; Tall Tale is once per Player/playthrough.\n- Journal reentry: once per route entry, never a progression acknowledgment.\n- Automatic progression events: once per `(Player or membership, eventId, policyVersion)`.\n- Pause/resume: once per immutable transition event/state version.\n- Undo: once per `STATE_REVERTED` event.\n- Non-looping ink: once per presentation instance at its semantic label.\n- Section-local enhancement: once per event, section target, and authoritative state version.\n- Manual replay: unlimited policy-approved attempts; must never rewrite the automatic one-shot receipt.\n\nA failed, invisible, aborted, interrupted, timed-out, or ownership-rejected mandatory attempt must leave this key unconsumed.\n\n## Test protocol and isolation\n\nUnit tests:\n\n- Exhaustive `Record<PlayerProgressionEventType, Policy>` so a new Player event fails typecheck.\n- Pure queue reducer with fake clock: ordering, dedupe, collision, preemption, retry bounds, stale events, replay arbitration.\n- One-shot state machine and acknowledgment eligibility for every terminal outcome.\n- Pause/resume collapse and undo summaries.\n- Player-safe replay-envelope privacy sentinels.\n\nComponent tests:\n\n- Fake EventSource, fetch, Director, audio, focus, and visibility.\n- Every interruption in Phase 3 §39.\n- Duplicate ID produces no scene/audio/ack.\n- Replay cannot preempt live.\n- Live preempts replay only through a declared semantic boundary.\n- Remount/reconnect restores unacknowledged mandatory work.\n- Revocation proves zero retry timers, empty queue, cleared content, stopped audio, and terminal focus.\n- Concurrent reading-state writes require CAS/version or a dedicated row.\n\nIntegration tests:\n\n- Use a unique isolated database; never the shared canonical database.\n- Test backlog/listener race, `Last-Event-ID`, out-of-order batches, lost acknowledgment response, membership revocation, and idempotent pause/resume.\n- Assert exact event rows, acknowledgment rows, sequence values, and absence of mutation during replay.\n- Verify Player event allowlists against every stored event type.\n\nE2E:\n\n- Mutation workflows in serialized Chromium only;
